**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
```

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching

# Chromium Blink Rendering Pipeline: Style to Paint

## Your Task

Trace how a CSS style change propagates through Chromium's Blink rendering engine. Find the key C++ source files in `chromium/chromium` that implement the rendering pipeline stages: 1. The file under `third_party/blink/renderer/core/css/resolver/` that implements `StyleResolver` — the class that resolves computed styles for DOM elements. 2. The file under `third_party/blink/renderer/core/layout/` that defines `LayoutObject` — the base class for the layout tree. 3. The file that implements `PaintLayer` — the painting layer abstraction under `third_party/blink/renderer/core/paint/`. 4. The file that defines `DisplayItemList` or `PaintController` — the display list that records paint operations. Report each file path and key class name.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/chromium--2d05e315` (chromium/chromium)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've successfully traced the CSS style change propagation through Chromium's Blink rendering engine and created the answer file.

## Summary of Findings

I've identified the four key C++ source files that implement the Blink rendering pipeline stages:

1. **StyleResolver** (`third_party/blink/renderer/core/css/resolver/style_resolver.h`, line 63)
   - Resolves computed styles for DOM elements based on stylesheets

2. **LayoutObject** (`third_party/blink/renderer/core/layout/layout_object.h`, line 270)
   - Base class for the layout tree, handles positioning and sizing

3. **PaintLayer** (`third_party/blink/renderer/core/paint/paint_layer.h`, line 174)
   - Painting layer abstraction for complex paint operations and compositing

4. **DisplayItemList** & **PaintController** 
   - `DisplayItemList` (line 28 in `paint_item_list.h`) - Container for paint operations
   - `PaintController` (line 131 in `paint_controller.h`) - Records and manages paint artifacts

The pipeline flows as: **Style (CSS) → Layout (geometry) → Paint Layers (grouping) → Display Items (recording operations)**

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, class symbols, and a detailed narrative explanation of the rendering pipeline.

kExcludeSelf };\\n75: \\n76: // Used in PaintLayerPaintOrderIterator.\\n77: enum PaintLayerIteration {\\n78:   kNegativeZOrderChildren = 1,\\n79:   // Normal flow children are not mandated by CSS 2.1 but are an artifact of\\n80:   // our implementation: we allocate PaintLayers for elements that\\n81:   // are not treated as stacking contexts and thus we need to walk them\\n82:   // during painting and hit-testing.\\n83:   kNormalFlowChildren = 1 << 1,\\n84:   kPositiveZOrderChildren = 1 << 2,\\n85: \\n86:   kStackedChildren = kNegativeZOrderChildren | kPositiveZOrderChildren,\\n87: `invisible_for_position_visibility_`.\\n96: enum class LayerPositionVisibility : uint8_t {\\n97:   // anchors-visible, anchor intersection.\\n98:   kAnchorsIntersectionVisible = 1,\\n99:   // anchors-visible, anchor CSS visibility.\\n100:   kAnchorsCssVisible = 1 << 1,\\n101:   // anchors-visible, chained anchor visibility.\\n102:   kChainedAnchorsVisible = 1 << 2,\\n103:   // no-overflow.\\n104:   kNoOverflow = 1 << 3,\\n105: };\\n106: \\n107: // PaintLayer is an old object that handles lots of unrelated operations.\\n108: //\\n109: // We want it to die at some point and be replaced by more focused objects,\\n110: // which would remove (or at least compartmentalize) a lot of complexity.\\n111: // See the STATUS OF PAINTLAYER section below.\\n112: //\\n113: // The class is central to painting and hit-testing. That's because it handles\\n114: // a lot of tasks (we included ones done by associated satellite objects for\\n115: // historical reasons):\\n116: // - Complex painting operations (opacity, clipping, filters, reflections, ...).\\n117: // - hardware acceleration (through PaintLayerCompositor).\\n118: // - scrolling (through PaintLayerScrollableArea).\\n119: // - some performance optimizations.\\n120: //\\n121: // The compositing code is also based on PaintLayer. The entry to it is the\\n122: // PaintLayerCompositor, which fills |composited_layer_mapping| for hardware\\n123: // accelerated layers.\\n124: //\\n125: // TODO(jchaffraix): Expand the documentation about hardware acceleration.\\n126: //\\n127: //\\n128: // ***** SELF-PAINTING LAYER *****\\n129: // One important concept about PaintLayer is \\\"self-painting\\\"\\n130: // (is_self_painting_layer_).\\n131: // PaintLayer started as the implementation of a stacking context. This meant\\n132: // that we had to use PaintLayer's painting order (the code is now in\\n133: // PaintLayerPainter and PaintLayerStackingNode) instead of the LayoutObject's\\n134: // children order. Over the years, as more operations were handled by\\n135: // PaintLayer, some LayoutObjects that were not stacking context needed to have\\n136: // a PaintLayer for bookkeeping reasons. One such example is the overflow hidden\\n137: // case that wanted hardware acceleration and thus had to allocate a PaintLayer\\n138: // to get it. However overflow hidden is something LayoutObject can paint\\n139: // without a PaintLayer, which includes a lot of painting overhead. Thus the\\n140: // self-painting flag was introduced. The flag is a band-aid solution done for\\n141: // performance reason only. It just brush over the underlying problem, which is\\n142: // that its design doesn't match the system's requirements anymore.\\n143: //\\n144: // Note that the self-painting flag determines how we paint a LayoutObject:\\n145: // - If the flag is true, the LayoutObject is painted through its PaintLayer,\\n146: //   which is required to apply complex paint operations. The paint order is\\n147: //   handled by PaintLayerPainter::paintChildren, where we look at children\\n148: //   PaintLayers.\\n149: // - If the flag is false, the LayoutObject is painted like normal children (ie\\n150: //   as if it didn't have a PaintLayer). The paint order is handled by\\n151: //   BoxFragmentPainter.\\n152: // This means that the self-painting flag changes the painting order in a subtle\\n153: // way, which can potentially have visible consequences. Those bugs are called\\n154: // painting inversion as we invert the order of painting for 2 elements\\n155: // (painting one wrongly in front of the other).\\n156: // See https://crbug.com/370604 for an example.\\n157: //\\n158: //\\n159: // ***** STATUS OF PAINTLAYER *****\\n160: // We would like to remove this class in the future. The reasons for the removal\\n161: // are:\\n162: // - it has been a dumping ground for features for too long.\\n163: // - it is the wrong level of abstraction, bearing no correspondence to any CSS\\n164: //   concept.\\n165: //\\n166: // Its features need to be migrated to helper objects. This was started with the\\n167: // introduction of satellite objects: PaintLayer*. Those helper objects then\\n168: // need to be moved to the appropriate LayoutObject class, probably to a rare\\n169: // data field to avoid growing all the LayoutObjects.\\n170: //\\n171: // A good example of this is PaintLayerScrollableArea, which can only happen\\n172: // be instanciated for LayoutBoxes. With the current design, it's hard to know\\n173: // that by reading the code.\\n174: class CORE_EXPORT PaintLayer : public GarbageCollected<PaintLayer>,\\n175:                                public DisplayItemClient {\\n176:  public:\\n177:   explicit PaintLayer(LayoutBoxModelObject*);\\n178:   PaintLayer(const PaintLayer&) = delete;\\n179:   PaintLayer& operator=(const PaintLayer&) = delete;\\n180:   ~PaintLayer() override;\\n181: \\n182:   void Destroy();\\n183: \\n184:   // DisplayItemClient methods\\n185:   String DebugName() const final;\\n186:   DOMNodeId OwnerNodeId() const final;\\n187: \\n188:   LayoutBoxModelObject& GetLayoutObject() const { return *layout_object_; }\\n189:   LayoutBox* GetLayoutBox() const {\\n190:     return DynamicTo<LayoutBox>(layout_object_.Get());\\n191:   }\\n192:   // Returns |GetLayoutBox()| if it exists and has fragments.\\n193:   const LayoutBox* GetLayoutBoxWithBlockFragments() const;\\n194: \\n195:   PaintLayer* Parent() const { return parent_.Get(); }\\n196:   PaintLayer* PreviousSibling() const { return previous_.Get(); }\\n197:   PaintLayer* NextSibling() const { return next_.Get(); }\\n198:   PaintLayer* FirstChild() const { return first_.Get(); }\\n199:   PaintLayer* LastChild() const { return last_.Get(); }\\n200: \\n201: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/chromium--2d05e315@524690a4542d3d93020fb4764b8ba5cc968d1a3d/-/blob/third_party/blink/renderer/core/paint/paint_layer.h%3FL1-200\"}",
